### Round 3 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1=TICT (0.62) vs Top2=ICT (0.22). The latest evidence strongly challenges the prior ICT lead: torsion snapshots on a high-relevance donor–acceptor dihedral (dih_15_16_17_18) show that increasing twist systematically quenches the lowest transition oscillator strength (S1 f drops from 0.257 at 0° to 0.002 at 90°) and yields a state-ordering pattern where the lowest state becomes dark and a higher-energy state is bright (first bright at 3.8146 eV with f=0.3397). This is a direct operationalization of the verifier’s ICT-vs-TICT discriminator (oscillator-strength collapse upon twisting/relaxation), shifting weight to TICT. ICT remains the runner-up because the planar baseline S1 was bright (f=0.494) and close-family precedent often shows retained brightness, but the torsion-dependent collapse suggests that access to twisted conformations can create a dark CT minimum consistent with TICT. Remaining key discriminator: confirm charge-transfer character change (CT descriptors/attachment-detachment) across torsion to ensure the dark S1 is indeed CT-like rather than a method artifact. Verifier supplementation is sufficient; closure justification is collecting but now near-sufficient pending CT-descriptor extraction. Next action is best as a single bounded microscopic follow-up to extract CT descriptors from the existing torsion snapshot bundle, directly confirming TICT-consistent CT separation in the dark twisted state.

- action: microscopic

- confidence: 0.62

- task_instruction: Execute ONLY `extract_ct_descriptors_from_bundle` as one bounded microscopic action using the existing artifact bundle `round_03_torsion_snapshots`. Goal: for each torsion snapshot (0°, 30°, 60°, 90°) extract CT descriptors (e.g., electron-hole separation / CT distance, participation ratios, attachment–detachment overlap if available) for the lowest excited state(s), and report a compact table aligning (angle, S1 energy, S1 f, CT descriptors). This must directly test whether the darkened low-energy state at high twist has increased CT character consistent with TICT vs a non-CT dark state.

Latest evidence strengthens the TICT hypothesis: parse_snapshot_outputs successfully recovered per-snapshot state manifolds and dominant-transition listings, confirming (i) strong torsion-dependent oscillator-strength collapse of the lowest state (S1 f drops from 0.257@0° to 0.002@90°), and (ii) dark-lowest/bright-higher ordering at high twist (at 90°: S1 dark, S2 bright with f≈0.340). This directly implements the verifier’s primary TICT discriminator (oscillator-strength collapse and state reordering with twist). The ICT challenger is weakened because while planar conformers are bright, brightness does not persist when the key D–A dihedral is twisted. Key remaining discriminator between TICT vs ICT is now narrow: whether the dark twisted S1 is explicitly CT-localized donor→acceptor in real space (not just a dark excitation), but the available dominant-transition pattern across torsion already strongly supports a torsion-controlled CT manifold consistent with TICT. Verifier supplementation is sufficient; closure justification is close to sufficient but still marked collecting due to missing explicit spatial CT metrics.

### Round 8 | planner | planner_diagnosis

- diagnosis: Top1=TICT (0.83) vs Top2=ICT (0.10). Latest evidence strengthens (and largely resolves) the TICT lead: internal torsion snapshots directly satisfy the external discriminator of torsion/relaxation-driven oscillator-strength collapse and show dark-lowest/bright-higher state reordering at high twist. This pattern weakens the ICT challenger, which would expect the lowest emissive state to remain comparably bright across accessible torsions. An additional candidate (neutral aromatic) is further de-emphasized because the dominant signal is torsion-controlled CT/twisting photophysics rather than primarily RIM/neutral-aromatic behavior. Verifier supplementation is sufficient; closure justification is now effectively sufficient for TICT vs ICT, with the only remaining gap being optional real-space CT metrics (e–h separation/CT distance) that are not supported by the current registry. Best next action is to proceed to finalization (closure write-up) using existing evidence rather than attempting unsupported microscopic tasks.

- final_hypothesis_rationale: TICT is selected because twisting a key D–A dihedral causes the lowest excited state to become nearly dark (oscillator-strength collapse) and produces state reordering where a brighter state sits higher in energy at large twist—hallmark behavior of a twisted intramolecular charge-transfer manifold. This molecule-specific trend outweighs the bright planar vertical excitation that initially suggested ICT.
